  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;

  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;

  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */

  }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;

        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Couple of CLs in the work to look into the problems described in this issue:



<span class="line"><!---->Couple of CLs in the work to look into the problems described in this issue:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://crrev.com/c/3343870



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3343870"><!---->https://crrev.com/c/3343870<!----></a>



<br>





https://crrev.com/c/3351404



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3351404"><!---->https://crrev.com/c/3351404<!----></a>



<br>





https://crrev.com/c/3346109



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3346109"><!---->https://crrev.com/c/3346109<!----></a>



<br>





https://crrev.com/c/3345759



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/3345759"><!---->https://crrev.com/c/3345759<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





use-after-free triggered when task to create session log attempted to access member properties after the session_log_handler destructor called. Normally using a weak_pointer handles this however due to returning a result base::Unretained is being used. base::Unretrained expects the calling class to be responsible for ensuring lifecycle is managed[1]. An internal task_runner is being added to ensure the task's sequence lifetime is tied to the lifetime of the class.



<span class="line"><!---->use-after-free triggered when task to create session log attempted to access member properties after the session_log_handler destructor called. Normally using a weak_pointer handles this however due to returning a result base::Unretained is being used. base::Unretrained expects the calling class to be responsible for ensuring lifecycle is managed[1]. An internal task_runner is being added to ensure the task's sequence lifetime is tied to the lifetime of the class.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The two other issues described are related to double trigger of the "create session log" activity and the select dialog not closing down properly.  For the first, additional logic needs to be added to avoid clicking on the save button while the log file is being built.  The latter is due to not notifying the select dialog that the destructor has been called (which is, according to comments in select_file_dialog.h, a responsibility of the calling class[2])



<span class="line"><!---->The two other issues described are related to double trigger of the "create session log" activity and the select dialog not closing down properly.  For the first, additional logic needs to be added to avoid clicking on the save button while the log file is being built.  The latter is due to not notifying the select dialog that the destructor has been called (which is, according to comments in select_file_dialog.h, a responsibility of the calling class[2])<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->ref:<!----></span>

https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/refs/heads/main/docs/callback.md#binding-a-class-method-with-manual-lifetime-management



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/refs/heads/main/docs/callback.md#binding-a-class-method-with-manual-lifetime-management"><!---->https://chromium.googlesource.com/chromium/src/+/refs/heads/main/docs/callback.md#binding-a-class-method-with-manual-lifetime-management<!----></a>



<br>

So if the user is doing the diagnostic process and closes the current process, it will trigger UaF (see the new video on the attachment). 



<span class="line"><!---->), but after I observed that closing the browser is not necessary. UaF occurs because there is no checking outlives of the diagnostics and select_file_dialog_extension functions. So if the user is doing the diagnostic process and closes the current process, it will trigger UaF (see the new video on the attachment). <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Shutting down the diagnostics should properly reset all scoped elements and stop observing everything. This is because the shutdown may be due to the destruction of the window being proceeded, so we can no longer access it. But the diagnostics object is kept alive until processing is actually finalized.



<span class="line"><!---->Shutting down the diagnostics should properly reset all scoped elements and stop observing everything. This is because the shutdown may be due to the destruction of the window being proceeded, so we can no longer access it. But the diagnostics object is kept alive until processing is actually finalized.<!----></span>



<br>
